**无轨电车系统列表**，列出世界各城市运营中及已停运的[无轨电车系统](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/无轨电车 "wikilink")。

## 非洲

| [君士坦丁](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/君士坦丁_\(阿爾及利亞\) "wikilink") |         | /          | /       | 1914年開工，未完工 |
| 1921                                                            | 1963（？） |            |         |             |

###

| 系统名称 | 城市                                                            | 运营日期        | 停运日期       | 备注                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            |
| ---- | ------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------- | ---------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |

|      | [Medellín](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medellín "wikilink") | 12日10月1929年 | 1951年      | Also: An experimental trolleybus line, using one vehicle, operated on the campus of the [Universidad Pontificia Bolivariana](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pontifical_Bolivarian_University "wikilink") from 30日11月2011 until日12月2012.\[49\] A trolleybus system for Medellín is proposed (as of 2013).\[50\] |
|      |                                                               |             |            |                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               |

###

| 系统名称 | 城市                                                                     | 运营日期        | 停运日期 | 备注                        |
| ---- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------- | ---- | ------------------------- |
|      | ([La Habana](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Havana "wikilink") /Havana) | (18日9月1949) | ?    | Test operation, see note. |
|      |                                                                        |             |      |                           |

  - **Note**: Tests began 18日9月1949 along
    [tramway](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/tram "wikilink") lines using
    "all-service vehicles" ([dual-mode
    buses](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/dual-mode_bus "wikilink"))
    purchased secondhand from [Newark, New
    Jersey](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Newark,_New_Jersey "wikilink"),
    [US](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_of_America "wikilink").
    The tests did not involve building new or converting existing supply
    because Havana's tramway had twin-wire overhead. Regular service was
    not operated.

  - **Note**: The Mexico City trolleybus system was long thought to have
    opened in日4月1952, but is now known to have opened more than a year
    earlier, in日3月1951.\[53\]\[54\] Previous to that, there was an
    experimental line, for testing without passengers, in 1947 or 1948.

## California

| Name of System                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               | Location                                                                        | Date (From)       | Date (To)                                                                                                                                           | Notes                                                                                                                                                       |
| ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
|                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              | [Los Angeles](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles "wikilink")             | 11 September 1910 | 1915                                                                                                                                                | An early commercial trolleybus system in the United States.\[56\]\[57\]\[58\] Later, there were 1922 and 1937 demonstrations of newer vehicles.\[59\]\[60\] |
| [Los Angeles Transit Lines](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Transit_Lines "wikilink") (1947–51); [Los Angeles Metropolitan Transit Authority](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Metropolitan_Transit_Authority "wikilink") (1951–63)\[61\] | 3 August 1947                                                                   | 30 March 1963     | Construction of a new system was planned in the early 1990s, but the plans were cancelled in December 1993 because of a severe budget crisis.\[62\] |                                                                                                                                                             |
|                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              | ([Oakland](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oakland,_California "wikilink"))       |                   |                                                                                                                                                     | Construction started 1945, not completed. Vehicles built for Oakland were used in Los Angeles.                                                              |
|                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              | **[San Francisco](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/San_Francisco "wikilink")**     | 6 October 1935    |                                                                                                                                                     | See note, and see also [Trolleybuses in San Francisco](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trolleybuses_in_San_Francisco "wikilink").                             |
|                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              | ([Wrightwood](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wrightwood,_California "wikilink")) |                   |                                                                                                                                                     | See note.                                                                                                                                                   |
|                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              |                                                                                 |                   |                                                                                                                                                     |                                                                                                                                                             |

  - **Note** for Los Angeles: First system connected [Sunset
    Boulevard](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sunset_Boulevard "wikilink")
    with a new housing development, "Bungalow Town," in [Laurel
    Canyon](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Laurel_Canyon,_Los_Angeles "wikilink").
    Built and operated by Laurel Canyon Utilities Company.\[63\]
  - **Note** for San Francisco: The first trolleybus line was opened by
    the former [Market Street Railway
    Company](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Market_Street_Railway_Company "wikilink")
    (MSR). The [San Francisco Municipal
    Railway](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/San_Francisco_Municipal_Railway "wikilink")
    ("Muni") opened the second trolleybus line on 7 September 1941. MSR
    was absorbed by Muni on 29 September 1944. Most of the current
    trolleybus system was built to replace MSR tramway lines.
  - **Note** for Wrightwood: Line planned ca. 1911 by Lone Pine
    Utilities Company, an affiliate of Laurel Canyon Utilities Company
    (q.v., above). Planned to connect Grava railway station (or halt) to
    Wrightwood. A contemporary account in a local newspaper states that
    construction was started but not completed.

## New Jersey

| Name of System | Location                                                              | Date (From)       | Date (To)        | Notes                               |
| -------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------- | ---------------- | ----------------------------------- |
|                | [Camden](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Camden,_New_Jersey "wikilink") | 1 September 1935  | 1 June 1947      | "All-Service Vehicle" (ASV) system. |
|                | [Newark](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Newark,_New_Jersey "wikilink") | 15 September 1935 | 10 November 1948 | "All-Service Vehicle" (ASV) system. |
|                |                                                                       |                   |                  |                                     |

  - **Notes** for Camden and Newark: The "All-Service Vehicle" systems
    used gasoline-electric motorbuses modified for operation from
    external power or onboard engine-generator set. The route systems
    were not fully electrified, and operating depots had no overhead
    wires. (A modern-day equivalent of this is the [dual-mode
    bus](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/dual-mode_bus "wikilink").)

The operator conducted a demonstration at
[Weehawken](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Weehawken_Township,_New_Jersey "wikilink")
in 1934 prior to opening of public service with ASVs in 1935. Weehawken
was served by the Newark system.

The Newark ASV system also served many adjacent towns, including the
[Hudson
County](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hudson_County,_New_Jersey "wikilink")
towns of
[Bayonne](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bayonne,_New_Jersey "wikilink"),
[Jersey
City](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jersey_City,_New_Jersey "wikilink"),
[Hoboken](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hoboken,_New_Jersey "wikilink"),
[Union
City](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Union_City,_New_Jersey "wikilink")
and [West New
York](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_New_York,_New_Jersey "wikilink"),
the [Passaic
County](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Passaic_County,_New_Jersey "wikilink")
towns of
[Passaic](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Passaic,_New_Jersey "wikilink")
and
[Paterson](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paterson,_New_Jersey "wikilink"),
and the [Union
County](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Union_County,_New_Jersey "wikilink")
towns of
[Elizabeth](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elizabeth,_New_Jersey "wikilink")
and
[Plainfield](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plainfield,_New_Jersey "wikilink").

## Ohio

| Name of System                                                                                              | Location                                                                | Date (From)      | Date (To)         | Notes                                                                                                             |
| ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------- | ---------------- | ----------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
|                                                                                                             | [Akron](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Akron,_Ohio "wikilink")           | 12 December 1941 | 6 June 1959       |                                                                                                                   |
|                                                                                                             | [Cincinnati](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cincinnati "wikilink")       | 1 December 1936  | 18 June 1965      |                                                                                                                   |
| <small>[Cleveland Transit System](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cleveland_Transit_System "wikilink")<small> | [Cleveland](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cleveland "wikilink")         | 1 March 1936     | 14 June 1963      |                                                                                                                   |
|                                                                                                             | [Columbus](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Columbus,_Ohio "wikilink")     | 3 December 1933  | 3 May 1965        |                                                                                                                   |
|                                                                                                             | **[Dayton](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dayton,_Ohio "wikilink")**     | 23 April 1933    |                   | See note, and see also [Trolleybuses in Dayton](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trolleybuses_in_Dayton "wikilink"). |
| <small>♦ Dayton Street Railway Company (Dayton Street Transit Company)</small>                              |                                                                         | 23 April 1933    | (28 April 1941)   | Sold to CRC.                                                                                                      |
| <small>♦ Oakwood Street Railway Company (Oakwood and Dayton Transit Company)</small>                        |                                                                         | 19 January 1936  | (1 October 1956)  | Sold to CTC.                                                                                                      |
| <small>♦ Peoples Railway Company (Peoples Transit Company)</small>                                          |                                                                         | 11 October 1936  | (9 March 1945)    | Sold to CRC.                                                                                                      |
| <small>♦ The City Railway Company (later: The City Transit Company, or CTC)</small>                         |                                                                         | 25 March 1938    |                   |                                                                                                                   |
| <small>♦ Dayton-Xenia Railway Company</small>                                                               |                                                                         | 1 October 1940   | (31 October 1955) | Sold to CTC.                                                                                                      |
|                                                                                                             | [Toledo](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Toledo,_Ohio "wikilink")         | 1 February 1935  | 28 May 1952       |                                                                                                                   |
|                                                                                                             | [Youngstown](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Youngstown,_Ohio "wikilink") | 11 November 1936 | 10 June 1959      |                                                                                                                   |
|                                                                                                             |                                                                         |                  |                   |                                                                                                                   |

  - **Note** for Dayton: Dayton was a notable exception to the "typical"
    U.S. trend of consolidation ("unification") of public transport
    services. Five companies operated tramway service from 1909 to 1933.
    All five companies operated trolleybuses for several months in
    1940–41, prior to the beginning of consolidations. The largest
    company, the City Railway Company (CRC), became the City Transit
    Company (CTC) in 1955 and was taken into public ownership by the
    Miami Valley Regional Transit Authority in 1972. MVRTA is known
    today as the [Greater Dayton Regional Transit
    Authority](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greater_Dayton_Regional_Transit_Authority "wikilink").

<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><p>Seattle Transit System (until 1973);<br />
<a href="https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/King_County_Metro" title="wikilink">Metro</a> (1973 to pres)</p></td>
<td><p><strong><a href="https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seattle" title="wikilink">Seattle</a></strong></p></td>
<td><p>28 April 1940</p></td>
<td><p> </p></td>
<td><p>Also 27 February 1937 - 9 March 1937 demonstration. All service suspended 21 January 1978 – 14 September 1979 for renewal; see note.<br />
See also <a href="https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trolleybuses_in_Seattle" title="wikilink">Trolleybuses in Seattle</a>.</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

  - **Note** for Seattle: All overhead wires, other infrastructure and
    vehicles (but not most support poles for the wires) were replaced
    during the 1978–79 suspension, but the transition is not considered
    the end of one system and the beginning of a "second" system,
    because the suspension was only temporary, for upgrading. The
    current system is widely considered as having opened in 1940.\[76\]

[Dual-mode](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dual-mode_bus "wikilink")
(diesel-trolley) buses operated 15 September 1990 - 24 January 2005 on
routes using the [Downtown Seattle Transit
Tunnel](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metro_Bus_Tunnel_\(Seattle\) "wikilink").
The overhead wire system in the tunnel was not connected to that used by
surface trolleybus services.

**Notes** for the two tunnel trolleybus lines:

  - The 6.1 km [Kanden Tunnel
    Trolleybus](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kanden_Tunnel_Trolleybus "wikilink")
    line operates almost entirely in tunnel, through a mountain, and
    connects Ōgizawa Station with Kurobe Dam, for tourists and hikers.
    Ōgizawa Station is in [Ōmachi
    city](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ōmachi,_Nagano "wikilink"),
    [Nagano
    Prefecture](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nagano_Prefecture "wikilink").
  - The affiliated 3.6 km [Tateyama Tunnel
    Trolleybus](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tateyama_Tunnel_Trolleybus "wikilink")
    line, similarly, operates entirely in tunnel and connects Daikanbo
    with Murodō. The line is located in [Tateyama
    town](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tateyama,_Toyama "wikilink"),
    [Toyama
    Prefecture](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Toyama_Prefecture "wikilink").

Both lines are part of the [Tateyama Kurobe Alpine
Route](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tateyama_Kurobe_Alpine_Route "wikilink").
This passes through [Chūbu-Sangaku National
Park](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chūbu-Sangaku_National_Park "wikilink")
(also known in English as "Japan Alps National Park").

## **

| Name of System | Location                                                            | Date (From) | Date (To)   | Notes                                                                                                                      |
| -------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------- | ----------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
|                | [Forbach](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Forbach "wikilink")         | 19 May 1951 | 1 Nov 1969  |                                                                                                                            |
|                | [Metz](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metz "wikilink")               | 14 Sep 1947 | 30 Apr 1966 |                                                                                                                            |
|                | **[Nancy](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nancy,_France "wikilink")** | 27 Sep 1982 |             | [Dual-mode](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dual-mode_bus "wikilink") (trolley/diesel) operation until about 2000. See note. |
|                |                                                                     |             |             |                                                                                                                            |

  - **Note** for Nancy: *TVR* opened 28 Jan 2001,\[117\] replacing
    dual-mode bus operation. Operation suspended 9 Mar 2001 - 13 Mar
    2002 because of technical problems. *TVR*, Transport sur Voie
    Réservée, is the [Guided Light
    Transit](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bombardier_Guided_Light_Transit "wikilink")
    system, using a centre guide rail and marketed as "Trams sur pneus"
    (trams on tyres). In Nancy, TVR surface guidance only covers a
    portion of the route, and the vehicles are able to operate away from
    the guide rail in electric mode, using [trolley
    poles](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/trolley_pole "wikilink"), and
    thus the system is trolleybus,\[118\] despite the Nancy operator's
    marketing it as the *tram*. TVR systems elsewhere use
    [pantographs](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/pantograph_\(rail\) "wikilink"),
    and consequently are not commonly regarded as trolleybus systems
    (see note at bottom of list).\[119\]\[120\]

###

See *Asia* section of list, above. Although trolleybuses served the
European part of
[Istanbul](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Istanbul "wikilink"), the
country's two other trolleybus systems were located in the Asian part of
Turkey.

###  (Territories only, in Oceania)

####  (Territory of)

| 系统名称                                   | 城市                                                                    | 运营日期  | 停运日期 | 备注            |
| -------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------- | ----- | ---- | ------------- |
| Honolulu Rapid Transit Company Limited | [Honolulu](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Honolulu,_Hawaii "wikilink") | 1936年 | \-   | Demonstration |
| 1日1月1938年                              | 22日6月1957年                                                            |       |      |               |

  - **Note**: The trolleybus system existed only in the period before
    [Hawaii](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Territory_of_Hawaii "wikilink")
    became a [U.S.
    state](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S._state "wikilink"). For
    convenience, it is also included in [List of trolleybus systems in
    the United
    States](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_trolleybus_systems_in_the_United_States#Hawaii_\(Territory_of\) "wikilink").

## 参考资料

## 书籍

  - Gregoris, Paolo; Rizzoli, Francesco; and Serra, Claudio. 2003. "Giro
    d'Italia in filobus" (ISBN 88-7785-193-7). Cortona: Editore Calosci.
  - Jones, David. Australian Trolleybuses. Wellington: City Tramway
    Publications.
  - Mackinger, Gunter. 1979. "Obus in Österreich" (ISBN 3-900134-62-6).
    (*Eisenbahn-Sammelheft Nr. 16.*) Wien: Verlag Slezak.
  - Millar, Sean. 1986. "Trolleybuses in New Zealand" (ISBN
    0-908726-20-1). Auckland: Millar Publishing.
  - Murray, Alan. 2000. "World Trolleybus Encyclopaedia" (ISBN
    0-904235-18-1). Yateley, Hampshire, UK: Trolleybooks.
  - Pabst, Martin. 1989. "Tram & Trolley in Africa" (ISBN
    3-88490-152-4). Krefeld: Röhr Verlag GMBH.
  - Peschkes, Robert. "World Gazetteer of Tram, Trolleybus, and Rapid
    Transit Systems."
      - *Part One, Latin America* (ISBN 1-898319-02-2). 1980. Exeter,
        UK: Quail Map Company.
      - *Part Two, Asia+USSR / Africa / Australia* (ISBN 0-948619-00-7).
        1987. London: Rapid Transit Publications.
      - *Part Three, Europe* (ISBN 0-948619-01-5). 1993. London: Rapid
        Transit Publications.
      - *Part Four, North America* (ISBN 0-948619-06-6). 1998. London:
        Rapid Transit Publications.
  - [Sebree, Mac](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mac_Sebree "wikilink"),
    and Paul Ward. 1974. "The Trolley Coach in North America"
    (Interurbans Special 59). Los Angeles:
    [Interurbans](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interurban_Press "wikilink").
  - Stock, Werner. 1987. "Obus-Anlagen in Deutschland" (ISBN
    3-926882-00-X). Bielefeld: Hermann Busch Verlag.
  - "Straßenbahnatlas ehem. Sowjetunion" / "Tramway Atlas of the former
    USSR" (ISBN 3-926524-15-4). 1996. Berlin: Arbeitsgemeinschaft
    Blickpunkt Straßenbahn, in conjunction with [Light Rail Transit
    Association](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Light_Rail_Transit_Association "wikilink"),
    London.
  - "Straßenbahnatlas Rumänien" (compiled by Andreas Günther, Sergei
    Tarkhov and Christian Blank; ISBN 3-926524-23-5). 2004. Berlin:
    Arbeitsgemeinschaft Blickpunkt Straßenbahn.
  - Tarkhov, Sergei. 2000. "Empire of the Trolleybus: Vol 1 - Russia"
    (ISBN 0-948619-02-3). London: Rapid Transit Publications.
  - 吉川文夫 (Yoshikawa, Fumio). 1995.　日本のトロリーバス (Nippon no "trolleybus")
    (ISBN 4-88548-066-3). Tokyo: kk Denkisha-kenkyûkai.

173. At a referendum held on 17 June 2007, the
     [cantonal](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cantons_of_Switzerland "wikilink")
     electorate rejected a proposal by trolleybus supporters for
     retention of the trolleybus system. The electorate accepted a
     counter-proposal by the cantonal authority to purchase motorbuses
     to replace the trolleybus fleet. Consequently, the only
     then-remaining trolleybus line closed in June 2008: [Referendum
     results](http://www.regierungsrat.bs.ch/07-06-17-kant-schlussresultat.pdf)

     Association (UK).
